<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1001118129">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1001118129" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/83144-el" class="left imgcol" title="El"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1452263504p2/83144.jpg" alt="El" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1001118129?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 29, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/83144-el" class="user" title="El">El</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7546430-neuromancer" title="Mass Market Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=20th-centurylit-late" class="actionLinkLite">20th-centurylit-late</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=1001-books-list" class="actionLinkLite">1001-books-list</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=society-went-boom" class="actionLinkLite">society-went-boom</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=science-fictiony" class="actionLinkLite">science-fictiony</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=library-borrow" class="actionLinkLite">library-borrow</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=biddles" class="actionLinkLite">biddles</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1001118129">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3156748770015564094">...snort...<br /><br />Excuse me; I just woke up. I've been essentially asleep since first picking this book up a few days ago. I had to keep smacking myself to stay awake.<br /><br />Cyberpunk. The matrix. Jacking in. Flipping. And on and on.<br /><br />The cover of my book blurbs <em>Washington Post</em>, which uses words like "kaleidoscopic, picaresque, flashy." You <strong>lie</strong>, <em>Washington Post</em>. There's none of that here. There is no flash.<br /><br />This is a story about drugs and computers and awkwardly phrased sex. (The sex itself isn't awkward, but it</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3156748770015564094">...snort...<br /><br />Excuse me; I just woke up. I've been essentially asleep since first picking this book up a few days ago. I had to keep smacking myself to stay awake.<br /><br />Cyberpunk. The matrix. Jacking in. Flipping. And on and on.<br /><br />The cover of my book blurbs <em>Washington Post</em>, which uses words like "kaleidoscopic, picaresque, flashy." You <strong>lie</strong>, <em>Washington Post</em>. There's none of that here. There is no flash.<br /><br />This is a story about drugs and computers and awkwardly phrased sex. (The sex itself isn't awkward, but it's written awkwardly, like Gibson thought he should add some sex.) This is an unemotional and fairly uninteresting book with uninteresting characters. I see a lot of people like it, and I know it's a classic of the genre, but I fail to see much in it. I'm not going to say it's the worst book I've ever read, thus the two stars, <em>but</em> this is a book for my real life book club and I'm fairly certain by tomorrow I won't remember much about this story at all. Which is a shame since our meeting isn't until a week from now. What is there even to discuss?<br /><br />Gibson wrote about stuff that wasn't really written about in the early-to-mid 80s, so there's that. And he coined the term <em>cyberpunk</em>. But there's so little to actually discuss here. The noirish aspects? I guess? Yeah, I could talk about that. As in "I liked the noirish aspects."<br /><br />Looking back at my notes, I see last July at this same time the same book club was reading <a title="Rendezvous with Rama (Rama, #1) by Arthur C. Clarke" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/112537.Rendezvous_with_Rama__Rama___1_">Rendezvous with Rama</a>. What is it with our normally awesome book club choosing boring science fiction novels to read for July?<br /><br />She flipped.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3156748770015564094">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_733401423">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/733401423" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/9246169-wanda" class="left imgcol" title="Wanda"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1441213786p2/9246169.jpg" alt="Wanda" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/733401423?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 08, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/9246169-wanda" class="user" title="Wanda">Wanda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=speculative-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=canadian-eh" class="actionLinkLite">canadian-eh</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=reading-project" class="actionLinkLite">reading-project</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=1980s" class="actionLinkLite">1980s</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=cbc-100-cdn-novels" class="actionLinkLite">cbc-100-cdn-novels</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=1001-books" class="actionLinkLite">1001-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=1000-guardian" class="actionLinkLite">1000-guardian</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=read-in-2015" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer733401423">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8885627038493332083">I can certainly see where <em>Neuromancer</em> was important in the 1980s when it was published. It brings together many threads of literature and assembles a lot of ideas that hadn’t previously been combined. There is the drug culture and general aura of darkness of Philip K. Dick’s fiction; the technology of Spider Robinson’s <em>Mindkiller</em>; the emergent machine intelligence foreshadowed by Heinlein’s <em>The Moon is a Harsh Mistress</em>; the “heist” elements of the story. For me, it also had faint echoes of <em>Dhalg</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8885627038493332083">I can certainly see where <em>Neuromancer</em> was important in the 1980s when it was published. It brings together many threads of literature and assembles a lot of ideas that hadn’t previously been combined. There is the drug culture and general aura of darkness of Philip K. Dick’s fiction; the technology of Spider Robinson’s <em>Mindkiller</em>; the emergent machine intelligence foreshadowed by Heinlein’s <em>The Moon is a Harsh Mistress</em>; the “heist” elements of the story. For me, it also had faint echoes of <em>Dhalgren</em>, with the whole “degeneration of society” aspect. I can also see where <em>Neuromancer</em> and <em>Blade Runner</em> both had influence on The Matrix movies.<br /><br />The idea of computer hacking was fresher in the 80s—the mass media was just starting to catch on to what it was and who was involved in it. <em>Neuromancer</em> explores possible future implications of hacking, including being able to directly wire one’s self into cyberspace or to eavesdrop on/ride along with augmented people. The bulkiness of the gear required to do this is shocking to 21st century sensibilities—our hardware just keeps getting more compact. This is one of the aspects of the book that truly ages it.<br /><br />There are lots ideas that were au courant then that really haven’t turned into mainstream items. Despite a lot of work, no one has managed to create a sentient artificial intelligence, so we don’t need a Turing Law Code to govern such things. It was a great idea on Gibson’s part, however. Space habitats that are easily accessed and cryogenics are still fiction at this point as well. <br /><br />I was struck by Case’s disparagement of his “meat,” his physical body. Our physical selves have their limitations, but they are also the sources of our greatest comforts—food, sleep, sex—and I’m unsure that we would feel the same emotions without our brain structures to support them. I, for one, have no desire to ever be uploaded to a machine—like the Flatliner Dixie that Case works with, I hope to cease to exist when my time comes.<br /><br />I give high marks for the world building—I felt like I could actually envision the dark corners of The Sprawl. Somewhat depressing is the fact that so many people are still living on the edge, scrambling to make enough cash to support themselves. So much for the happy, prosperous futures envisioned in earlier science fiction.<br /><br />This is book number 188 in my science fiction &amp; fantasy reading project.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8885627038493332083">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_205133536">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/205133536" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3025547-mike" class="left imgcol" title="Mike"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1446412780p2/3025547.jpg" alt="Mike" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/205133536?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 10, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3025547-mike" class="user" title="Mike">Mike</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3025547-mike?shelf=science-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3025547-mike?shelf=hugo-award-winner" class="actionLinkLite">hugo-award-winner</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3025547-mike?shelf=nebula-award-winner" class="actionLinkLite">nebula-award-winner</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3025547-mike?shelf=speculative-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3025547-mike?shelf=computers" class="actionLinkLite">computers</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3025547-mike?shelf=cyberspace" class="actionLinkLite">cyberspace</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3025547-mike?shelf=virtual-reality" class="actionLinkLite">virtual-reality</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3025547-mike?shelf=artificial-intelligence" class="actionLinkLite">artificial-intelligence</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3025547-mike?shelf=cyber-punk" class="actionLinkLite">cyber-punk</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3025547-mike?shelf=matrix" class="actionLinkLite">matrix</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3025547-mike?shelf=dystopian" class="actionLinkLite">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer205133536">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer166844948774058598">The word "cyberspace" did not exist until William Gibson coined the phrase in his short story, "Burning Chrome," published in Omni Magazine in 1982. He also used the term in "Johnny Mnemonic," yes, the source of the Johnny Depp movie. And in Johnny Mnemonic, Gibson introduced an enhanced female street samurai named Molly Millions. She reappears as one of the main characters in "Neuromancer" in 1984. And it was with the publication of his debut novel that the use of the word "cyberspace" went vir</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText166844948774058598">The word "cyberspace" did not exist until William Gibson coined the phrase in his short story, "Burning Chrome," published in Omni Magazine in 1982. He also used the term in "Johnny Mnemonic," yes, the source of the Johnny Depp movie. And in Johnny Mnemonic, Gibson introduced an enhanced female street samurai named Molly Millions. She reappears as one of the main characters in "Neuromancer" in 1984. And it was with the publication of his debut novel that the use of the word "cyberspace" went viral. Gibson won the Hugo, Nebula, and the Phillip K. Dick Award for "Neuromancer."<br /><br />Oddly enough, Gibson composed his groundbreaking dystopian novel on a typewriter, not a qwerty keyboard. The world wide web was almost a decade away.<br /><br />At some point in the future, hacker Henry Case has committed the ultimate mistake. He has stolen from his employers. As punishment, he is chemically injected to prevent him from ever being able to access the virtual world of cyberspace.<br /><br />Down and out, Case grinds out a miserable living in the underworld of Chiba City in Japan. It is there where he is recruited by a shady character named Armitage who offers to pay for Cases cure, enabling him to re-enter the Matrix. There's a catch, of course. Case must offer his services as a hacker to Armitage who is never clear on exactly what job he wants Case to do.<br /><br />Gibson has tagged society simply as "the Sprawl." It is a disaffected, dystopian world. Greed is the primary motivator for all human action. And cyberspace is the vehicle by which to obtain whatever you want, if you've got the money to do it. Armitage does. Or, someone behind Armitage does.<br /><br />Think 1982's movie "Bladerunner," based on Phillip K. Dick's "Do Android Dream of Electric Sheep," and you have the perfect image of the world Gibson created. In fact, Gibson was about a third of the way through "Neuromancer" when "Bladerunner" premiered. The movie's release almost made Gibson pack in his typewriter. He felt he had been scooped.<br /><br />Today we loosely refer to cyberspace as what we know as the Internet. But cyberspace, in Gibson's creation is a world capable of perfect virtual reality.<br /><br />Computer deck cowboys like Case can jack into the matrix and "be" anywhere he needs to be. With the flip of a switch, he can experience the actual sensory observations of his sidekick, and for the course of the novel, his lover, Molly Millions. Molly has been implanted with a simstic. At one point, knowing that Case is "riding" with her, Molly teasingly circles the nipple of one of her breasts. Now, THAT's entertainment--at least for Case.<br /><br />Gibson's creation is masterful. Yet one is hard pressed to find anyone in "Neuromancer" a character that you comfortably indentify with--ellipsis added to avoid ending a sentence with a preposition. *ahem*<br /><br />Is "Neuromancer" a must read? Absolutely. Does it leave you hungry for more? Well, no, unless you breathlessly await the release of the next Hugo, Nebula, Dick, Campbell, or Locus award. Nihilism has been done before and better. A little Dostoevsky will do the trick every time. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="166844948774058598">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1280137634">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1280137634" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5885760-andrew-smith" class="left imgcol" title="Andrew Smith"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1445019627p2/5885760.jpg" alt="Andrew Smith" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1280137634?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 30, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5885760-andrew-smith" class="user" title="Andrew Smith">Andrew Smith</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5885760-andrew-smith?shelf=science-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5885760-andrew-smith?shelf=not-finished" class="actionLinkLite">not-finished</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1280137634">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13628613956974641836">The thing is I just didn’t get it. I like my SF near future and close enough to present day reality for me to be able to translate what we do now into what we’re supposed to be doing (or able to do) in the future. If it’s too wild, or just too big a leap, my mind doesn’t seem to allow me to make the jump. <br /><br />Then there’s the language thing. The use of a new vocabulary left me befuddled and confused. I just didn’t know what was going on most of the time. And when I did glean a bit of the narrative i</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13628613956974641836">The thing is I just didn’t get it. I like my SF near future and close enough to present day reality for me to be able to translate what we do now into what we’re supposed to be doing (or able to do) in the future. If it’s too wild, or just too big a leap, my mind doesn’t seem to allow me to make the jump. <br /><br />Then there’s the language thing. The use of a new vocabulary left me befuddled and confused. I just didn’t know what was going on most of the time. And when I did glean a bit of the narrative it just seemed to have been too much like hard work to get there. So that’s another thing, I like my fiction easy. Well no, not easy but understandable. I’ve coped with most of Murakami’s surreal tales and I love time travel books, so escape from reality isn’t a problem for me – in fact it’s a joy – but everyday life lived in an environment so alien, so different and (for me) so unbelievable is just a switch-off. <br /><br />A quick synopsis for anyone who hasn’t read the book:<br />Case is a hacker who has been ‘altered’ so he can’t hack any more. He lives life as a hustler in Japan until he gets an offer from a mysterious type who offers to restore his hacking ability in exchange for undertaking some work for him. Case is suspicious and, having teamed up with a modified female, he sets out to find out more about the man. The rest (as far as I could tell) was a sort of hardboiled detective tale but set in the netherworld of cyberspace. It also had a touch of <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0054047/"> The Magnificent Seven </a> about it. Though, in truth, I gave up at half way – my mind fried by terminology I couldn’t comprehend and a story that had jettisoned me and left me behind some time ago.<br /><br />On the up-side, I like Case who I found to be the archetypal street-smart hardass who is on his uppers but has sufficient moral compass to keep him from straying too far from the straight and narrow. I also enjoyed some of the brilliant descriptions – mainly of the cyberspace world – that pepper the book.<br /><br />Not my cup of tea but note my rating simply reflects the fact I didn’t finish it.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13628613956974641836">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_655927547">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/655927547" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8192509-gavin" class="left imgcol" title="Gavin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" alt="Gavin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/655927547?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 15, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8192509-gavin" class="user" title="Gavin">Gavin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=sci-fi" class="actionLinkLite">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer655927547">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3503219283868371758">It's sad to say, but Father Time has treated Neuromancer cruelly. I'm sure back in 1984, when this was first published, Gibson's take on the evolution of "cyberspace" was an innovative one. Hard for me to say for sure since I'm no computer expert and I was only 1 year old in 1984!. I can say that there is nothing innovative in Gibson's tale for the modern reader. <br /><br />That leaves the modern reader relying on the enjoyment of the story itself. Unfortunately that is average at best. The story revolves</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3503219283868371758">It's sad to say, but Father Time has treated Neuromancer cruelly. I'm sure back in 1984, when this was first published, Gibson's take on the evolution of "cyberspace" was an innovative one. Hard for me to say for sure since I'm no computer expert and I was only 1 year old in 1984!. I can say that there is nothing innovative in Gibson's tale for the modern reader. <br /><br />That leaves the modern reader relying on the enjoyment of the story itself. Unfortunately that is average at best. The story revolves around Henry Dorsett Case, a down on his luck criminal and former cyber cowboy, who is being blackmailed by vague and mysterious individuals into helping them with some corporate espionage. It has the feel of a sci-fi noir. The characters are hollow and unlikable. The real ones have no more personality than the AI's. There is some interesting ideas and the espionage and mystery does inspire a mild interest and curiosity but nothing more. The world building is decent. <br /><br />Gibson's writing style is also a problem, or it was for me. He throws the reader into the deep end of his world and forces them to learn a lot of the techno-babble by having the characters experience its sources. It's pretty confusing and does not make Neuromancer an easy read. The abrubt transition from scene to scene was another source of confusion. I also did not enjoy being drip feed bits of information about the characters while so much time was wasted on needless descriptions of stuff that was mostly irrelevant. <br /><br />I found this a pretty boring read. Still, it's better than the awful <a title="Snow Crash by Neal Stephenson" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/830.Snow_Crash">Snow Crash</a>, which was the last cyberpunk book I read, so that's a plus. <br /><br />Rating: 2.5 stars.<br /><br />Audio Note: The narrator was OK but I feel like this was not a book best suited to the audio medium. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3503219283868371758">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pJPMc8Ia4e96Yt7JNHlgs8TCogMGDd82G0fMNB4HLtnBR/OgMMj1Ffa6qnJKGIYBjTVhGk/QmJxxTsmm0pLYnA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/9226.William_Gibson">About William Gibson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/9226.William_Gibson"><img alt="9226" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1373826214p2/9226.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer1515328104484965311"><em>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name. <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces">See this thread for more information.</a></em><br /><br />William Ford Gibson is an American-Canadian writer who has been called the father of the cyberpunk subgenre of science fiction, having coined the term <em>cyberspace</em> in 1982 and popularized it in his first novel, <em>Neuromancer</em>(1984), which has sold more than 6.5 million copies wor</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1515328104484965311"><em>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name. <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces">See this thread for more information.</a></em><br /><br />William Ford Gibson is an American-Canadian writer who has been called the father of the cyberpunk subgenre of science fiction, having coined the term <em>cyberspace</em> in 1982 and popularized it in his first novel, <em>Neuromancer</em>(1984), which has sold more than 6.5 million copies worldwide.<br /><br />While his early writing took the form of short stories, Gibson has since written nine critically acclaimed novels (one in collaboration), contributed articles to several major publications, and has collaborated extensively with performance artists, filmmakers and musicians. His thought has been cited as an influence on science fiction authors, academia, cyberculture, and technology.<br /><br /><br />---------------------------------<br /><br /><em>William Gibson. (2007, October 17). In Wikipedia, The Free Encyclopedia. Retrieved 20:30, October 19, 2007, from <a rel="nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=William_Gibson&amp;oldid=165254323" target="_blank">http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?t...</a></em></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1515328104484965311">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/9226.William_Gibson" class="actionLink moreLink">More about William Gibson...</a>

a phantom entity who has plans for Mona, Angie, and all humanity, plans that cannot be controlled... or even known. And behind the intrigue lurks the shadowy Yakuza, the powerful Japanese underworld,       <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/909457-neuromancer">Quotes from Neuromancer</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“The sky above the port was the color of television, tuned to a dead channel.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/889-the-sky-above-the-port-was-the-color-of-television" class="actionLinkLite">453 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“Cyberspace. A consensual hallucination experienced daily by billions of legitimate operators, in every nation, by children being taught mathematical concepts... A graphic representation of data abstracted from banks of every computer in the human system. Unthinkable complexity. Lines of light ranged in the nonspace of the mind, clusters and constellations of data. Like city lights, receding...”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/14638-cyberspace-a-consensual-hallucination-experienced-daily-by-billions-of-legitimate" class="actionLinkLite">180 likes</a>
